<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I read it when I was 11 and FELL IN LOVE with horses and especially Flicka. It's an adult book, with adult themes, but all I saw was a boy and his<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I read it when I was 11 and FELL IN LOVE with horses and especially Flicka. It's an adult book, with adult themes, but all I saw was a boy and his beautiful horse. I read it every 10 years or so, and I see more of the depth ... relationships, struggle, anxiety, sacrifice, love, etc. As a 55 year old, I can still feel what I felt when I was 11 ... great book!<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_62870325">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62870325" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2465614-c" class="left imgcol" title="C"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1327009996p2/2465614.jpg" alt="C" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62870325?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 04, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2465614-c" class="user" title="C">C</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/164542.My_Friend_Flicka" title="Paperback 9780060512620" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2465614-c?shelf=junior-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">junior-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62870325">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17297108747941882059">If you've never been West around Colorado/Wyoming, O'Hara recreates it and captures it in her novels. I didn't realize just how well until I moved here and started recognizing the scenery.<br /><br />I've reread her books many times now and will likely reread them many more, hence the 5 stars. I've had to get rid of all my books a couple times in the past and have always felt like my shelves are incomplete till I've reacquired the Flicka set. <br /><br />O'Hara is a depression era writer and has a bit of "Steinbeck" fl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17297108747941882059">If you've never been West around Colorado/Wyoming, O'Hara recreates it and captures it in her novels. I didn't realize just how well until I moved here and started recognizing the scenery.<br /><br />I've reread her books many times now and will likely reread them many more, hence the 5 stars. I've had to get rid of all my books a couple times in the past and have always felt like my shelves are incomplete till I've reacquired the Flicka set. <br /><br />O'Hara is a depression era writer and has a bit of "Steinbeck" flavor to her writing. Not quite as harsh, but like fabric that wears over knees and elbows, it comes closer in some areas than others.<br /><br />There's more to the books than "a boy and his horse" story, and if you've only seen the movies I urge you to read the books instead. Nell's story is compelling reading, particularly her life philosophies she tries to impart on her sons. Rob's struggles to relate to his youngest son are a snapshot of how we approach the world on the terms we know and understand, and how difficult it is for us to step outside our understanding. <br /><br />I would suggest, after reading the books, to read up a bit on O'Hara herself. Quite a few parallels between her real life and the books, which may ultimately lend more insight into her and the characters she wrote. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17297108747941882059">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer887065133">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17379005868994420476">A tough-minded, wise, and beautiful book! (crossposted from amazon)<br /><br /><br />Like so many others, I read this book as a child, but I've reread it a couple of times as an adult - am doing so now. As my sister and other reviewers have said, this isn't "just" a horse story for children. It's a very adult, very sophisticated study of a young couple and their marriage. It's also a profound character study of their younger son, and the summer that his love for a filly forces him to take large steps toward matur</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17379005868994420476">A tough-minded, wise, and beautiful book! (crossposted from amazon)<br /><br /><br />Like so many others, I read this book as a child, but I've reread it a couple of times as an adult - am doing so now. As my sister and other reviewers have said, this isn't "just" a horse story for children. It's a very adult, very sophisticated study of a young couple and their marriage. It's also a profound character study of their younger son, and the summer that his love for a filly forces him to take large steps toward maturity. As a child, I identified strongly with 10-year-old Ken. As an adult, I still do - but I also empathize with his parents, who have to try to teach this brilliant, sensitive daydreamer how to accept responsibility and cope in the real world, All the characters in this book - human and animal - are three-dimensional and alive. Anyone who loves animal stories must read this book - you won't regret it. The natural world is shown in all its beauty and harshness, and O'Hara's prose is strong and clear. But it's the characters you'll remember forever.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17379005868994420476">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_857699307">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/857699307" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3429089-linda" class="left imgcol" title="Linda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442513224p2/3429089.jpg" alt="Linda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/857699307?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 19, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3429089-linda" class="user" title="Linda">Linda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2140474.My_Friend_Flicka" title="Hardcover 9780397009817" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3429089-linda?shelf=horses" class="actionLinkLite">horses</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer857699307">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3949438883472872455">Okay, I'll say it right here at the beginning of this review - for me: Best Horse Book Ever.<br /><br />In my quest as a young girl to read every single horse book I could find, I somehow bypassed this one. Maybe it was because I would appreciate it even more later in life. Although parts of it now seem dated (it was first published in 1941) it reads best as historical fiction, depicting life on a remote Wyoming ranch in the early part of the 20th century. Some things, like certain expressions and horse tra</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3949438883472872455">Okay, I'll say it right here at the beginning of this review - for me: Best Horse Book Ever.<br /><br />In my quest as a young girl to read every single horse book I could find, I somehow bypassed this one. Maybe it was because I would appreciate it even more later in life. Although parts of it now seem dated (it was first published in 1941) it reads best as historical fiction, depicting life on a remote Wyoming ranch in the early part of the 20th century. Some things, like certain expressions and horse training methods, might seem harsh to modern readers, but were real at the time.<br /><br />The theme of family, however, with a demanding father trying to balance the duties of running a ranch with understanding his sensitive son, buffered by a loving mother, ring just as true today as they must have when this book was first published.<br /><br />Oh, but for the love of a horse! A filly named Flicka. I think anyone who has ever truly loved an animal will relate to the passion that young Ken feels for his horse. I sobbed throughout this book, as Mary O'Hara's words went right to my heart all these decades later. Amazing, isn't it? The power of the written word.<br /><br />Horse lovers, animal lovers, and readers of historical fiction, don't miss this classic read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3949438883472872455">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14146435174707316784">Wow. What a boring book. <br /><br />Like any horse obsessed person, I try to see every horse-related movie and read nearly every horse related book. So, perhaps in this case, the mistake I made was that I watched the movie first and then read the book. <br />In the movie: 16 yo girl is misunderstood by her father. She fails final exam. Father is angry at her and doesn't want her to do anything fun except rewrite her essay so that she'll pass. Girl finds wild mustang. Girl catches mustang. Father is angry; doesn'</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14146435174707316784">Wow. What a boring book. <br /><br />Like any horse obsessed person, I try to see every horse-related movie and read nearly every horse related book. So, perhaps in this case, the mistake I made was that I watched the movie first and then read the book. <br />In the movie: 16 yo girl is misunderstood by her father. She fails final exam. Father is angry at her and doesn't want her to do anything fun except rewrite her essay so that she'll pass. Girl finds wild mustang. Girl catches mustang. Father is angry; doesn't want her to mess with it because it's dangerous and he considers it 'vermin'. Girl, of course, trains mustang anyway. Girl gets injured. Father becomes angrier. Girl continues training at night. Father sells mustang to rodeo. Girl is devastated. { insert heroic rodeo rescue here }<br /><br />The most I was expecting was a gender change and some minor tweaking on a few scenes, and maybe a little time change. But instead what I got was a whack in the face.<br />The movie is AHMAZING. And while most people say the book is always better than the movie, here's where I have to disagree. The movie = fast paced, exciting, keeps you on the edge of your seat, even brings tears. The book = So boring that by the end of a few pages I was asleep. I had to force myself to read this. The only reason I did keep on reading this was because a fellow horse loving friend of mine promised that by the end I'd be amazed.<br />Of course, the word amazement isn't even closely related to this book. You know how the adults in The Peanuts talk? "Wah wah, wah wah, wah wah." Right. Well, that's what this book was to me. I read it, yes, but it was just so lifeless that it barely came through to me. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4946439527788438039">I had read this book once before when I was quite a bit younger and didn't like it. I decided, however, that I'd put it back and try again when I was older. This time, reading it through, I actually did like it. I was rather surprised though, because I had heard it suggested as a children's book and I find it a bit more mature. I'd place it more in the young adults category, due to some language and subject matter.<br />This book is well known for being a sweet story about a boy and his horse, Flicka.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4946439527788438039">I had read this book once before when I was quite a bit younger and didn't like it. I decided, however, that I'd put it back and try again when I was older. This time, reading it through, I actually did like it. I was rather surprised though, because I had heard it suggested as a children's book and I find it a bit more mature. I'd place it more in the young adults category, due to some language and subject matter.<br />This book is well known for being a sweet story about a boy and his horse, Flicka. I, however, did not find that the most interesting relationship in the book. Instead,I found myself most interested in the chapters about the boy's father and mother. It is so hard to write a believable marriage and I think Mary O'Hara did that in this book. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15952469435696449966">My Friend Flika tells the story about Ken McLaughlin, who is the son of a Wyoming rancher and his horse Flika in 1941. Ken is a 10 year old boy who lives on a Wyoming ranch, the Goose Bar, with his father Rob, his mother Nell, and his brother Howard. The father sometimes gets very annoyed with Ken because he is a daydreamer. Ken returns home from boarding school with failing grades and has to repeat 5th grade. In order to be responsible Ken chooses a yearling to raise and this particular Filly h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15952469435696449966">My Friend Flika tells the story about Ken McLaughlin, who is the son of a Wyoming rancher and his horse Flika in 1941. Ken is a 10 year old boy who lives on a Wyoming ranch, the Goose Bar, with his father Rob, his mother Nell, and his brother Howard. The father sometimes gets very annoyed with Ken because he is a daydreamer. Ken returns home from boarding school with failing grades and has to repeat 5th grade. In order to be responsible Ken chooses a yearling to raise and this particular Filly has mustang blood in her which makes her a wild horse. She tries to escape the ranch and injures herself on barbed wire. Ken spends the rest of the summer nursing her back to health. Unfortunately, the horse gets a terrible blood infection but Ken spends a night in a shallow brook with her, nursing her back to health.<br /><br />I had a wonderful cat named Nadia. She had a terrible stomach infection and my mother and I took her to the veternarian to try and get her back to excellent health. Unfortunately her many trips to the hospital only temporarily got her better. In the end, she died of stomach cancer. I was devastated since she was my first pet.<br /><br />I loved this book and would give it 4 stars! I especially identified with the main protagonist, Ken because of his fearless devotion to Flicka. A child's bond to their first pet or animal is very deep and special and the love will stay with me forever. Since Nadia's death I have adopted a wonderful dog who brings us joy in the house every day. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15952469435696449966">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/654584-carol-edwards" class="user" title="Carol Edwards">Carol Edwards</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer25129802">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13832034374874790748">I think this book is my all time favorite. I say this because I have read it every 2 years or so since I was young. I can't really say that about any other book, although I am one of those people that will keep and reread, several times, books that I like. 'My Friend Flicka` is set on a ranch south west of Tie Siding, Wyoming. Since we live in this area the setting is familiar, even though things have changed a lot since 1941. Basically, it is your typical coming of age story, but it can interes</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13832034374874790748">I think this book is my all time favorite. I say this because I have read it every 2 years or so since I was young. I can't really say that about any other book, although I am one of those people that will keep and reread, several times, books that I like. 'My Friend Flicka` is set on a ranch south west of Tie Siding, Wyoming. Since we live in this area the setting is familiar, even though things have changed a lot since 1941. Basically, it is your typical coming of age story, but it can interest readers of all ages because it's not just about young Ken McLaughlin but his entire family, in particular, his mother, Nell. I like stories where most of the action takes place out of doors, and that go seriously into the relationships between humans and animals with care. Flicka is a really strong element in this story, with very well developed character and behavior. Still, there is so much practicality involved in the way the McLaughlin family and friends approach ranching and living in 1940's Wyoming that it doesn't ever really fall into the sentimental or maudlin. I only wish Mary O'Hara had written more books along this line, instead of going to Hollywood to write screenplays, or whatever it was she did. I always felt that Nell was almost too close to her, and that Nell's breakdown was actually Mary O'Hara's....less<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13832034374874790748">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18352375804132527193">I first read this book when I was eight or nine, and have wished for Wyoming ever since. It's a lovely story about a shy, dreamy kid who hates school and desperately wants his father's respect, but who can't help always doing something clumsy or forgetting something important.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText18352375804132527193">I first read this book when I was eight or nine, and have wished for Wyoming ever since. It's a lovely story about a shy, dreamy kid who hates school and desperately wants his father's respect, but who can't help always doing something clumsy or forgetting something important. For the summer, he wants nothing more than to have his own yearling colt to train. His father finally, reluctantly agrees--and Ken chooses the wildest, possibly most untrainable one of the bunch. <br /><br />This novel has such a sense of place and time, and to read it you must absolutely go outside. Climb a tree, or sprawl in the grass somewhere, hopefully someplace lonely with no cars or lawnmowers so that when you close your eyes, you can see mountains. Originally begun as a short story, O'Hara fleshed it out into something really wonderful. One of my all-time favorites.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1364772522?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 29, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/35474652-santorini" class="user" title="Santorini">Santorini</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1364772522">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17097807372540408044">I really wanted to love this book because I love horses, and I have always loved reading stories about them. It’s okay if you don’t mind lost of description, but I was disappointed.<br /><br />The pace was so incredibly slow that I was worried I would never finish this book. It dragged because of the amount of description coupled with problems with the plot. I understand why so much description was used because it does make you feel as if you are actually on a ranch in Wyoming, but I am much more of a dialo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17097807372540408044">I really wanted to love this book because I love horses, and I have always loved reading stories about them. It’s okay if you don’t mind lost of description, but I was disappointed.<br /><br />The pace was so incredibly slow that I was worried I would never finish this book. It dragged because of the amount of description coupled with problems with the plot. I understand why so much description was used because it does make you feel as if you are actually on a ranch in Wyoming, but I am much more of a dialog person, and I find it difficult to tolerate pages upon pages of long-winded descriptions. The problems I had with the plot were pretty straightforward. We all know the basic premise of this book. It’s about a horse named Flicka who becomes Ken’s friend. The problem I had was if we all basically know what is going to happen, then why don’t we actually encounter the horse until almost halfway through the novel? I was frustrated with this because I knew this thing was going to happen, but as I got to page 100, it still didn’t happen yet. Everything else was set up perfectly, and it took forever to finally get the story moving along. <br /><br />I wasn’t a big fan of Ken’s father, and not just in the “he-is-the-father-putting-too-much-pressure-on-his-son-way.” I found his character flip-flop a lot throughout the story. At first he didn’t want to help Ken, then he did, then he didn’t again, etc. It was very confusing because there was no basis given for him to be changing his opinions and actions like that.<br /><br />I did like Ken’s character though. He seemed almost imaginary; as if he wasn’t real, but he was someone I could sympathize with and root for until the end. I admired the hope and determination, but this couldn’t make up for the rest of the book. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17097807372540408044">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_217261236">

  <a href="/user/show/6505203-wendy" class="left imgcol" title="Wendy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439308300p2/6505203.jpg" alt="Wendy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/217261236?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6505203-wendy" class="user" title="Wendy">Wendy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6505203-wendy?shelf=horses-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">horses-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer217261236">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15255529291883999212">I was fortunate enough to read this as an adult, rather than as a child. Despite the simplistic writing and the fact that this is a 'boy and his horse' story, I don't believe this is really a book for children--at least not <em>young</em> children who have no parental guidance while reading.<br /><br />At least one horse dies fairly gruesomely, and while it isn't described in detail, it's made pretty clear that the horse bled to death during an operation to remove an undescended testicle. Oh, and this is just a page</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15255529291883999212">I was fortunate enough to read this as an adult, rather than as a child. Despite the simplistic writing and the fact that this is a 'boy and his horse' story, I don't believe this is really a book for children--at least not <em>young</em> children who have no parental guidance while reading.<br /><br />At least one horse dies fairly gruesomely, and while it isn't described in detail, it's made pretty clear that the horse bled to death during an operation to remove an undescended testicle. Oh, and this is just a page after it's described how nice and sweet that same horse is, and how much Ken likes it. Young children will probably be traumatized if they're not warned about this in advance, and/or if their parent doesn't take the time to explain it and comfort them. Also, Flicka herself is in grave danger several times during the book.<br /><br />Nevertheless, if the child is old enough and has an adult available to counsel them if necessary, I think they could handle it. It probably depends on the child and how sensitive they are.<br /><br />Having read it as an adult, the simplistic writing made it a fast, easy read. I enjoyed it, but I felt O'Hara was trying to say too many things within the same book, so the messages sort of got tangled up and lost in each other. In the end, I wasn't sure what her point was. All 'deeper meaning' aside, it's a pretty good story as well. Ken is fairly likable, and of course Flicka is a sweetheart.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15255529291883999212">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_302298256">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302298256" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8349963-marsha" class="left imgcol" title="Marsha"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1433802916p2/8349963.jpg" alt="Marsha" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/302298256?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 28, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8349963-marsha" class="user" title="Marsha">Marsha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7346832-my-friend-flicka" title=" 9780440961840" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8349963-marsha?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8349963-marsha?shelf=owned-books" class="actionLinkLite">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer302298256">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14151164961331288785">This is a book best suited for children, perhaps young girls who have themselves yearned for a horse or pony of their own. As an adult, at first I was irritated more often than not by the daydreaming useless Ken, who kept mumbling over and over again about getting a colt of his own, his smug older brother Howard, the irascible and overbearing father who apparently never outgrew his Army years and the yielding and almost saintlike mother. The range on which they lived was usually more enchanting</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14151164961331288785">This is a book best suited for children, perhaps young girls who have themselves yearned for a horse or pony of their own. As an adult, at first I was irritated more often than not by the daydreaming useless Ken, who kept mumbling over and over again about getting a colt of his own, his smug older brother Howard, the irascible and overbearing father who apparently never outgrew his Army years and the yielding and almost saintlike mother. The range on which they lived was usually more enchanting than the human characters on it. Its beauty and majesty were not to be denied as the author lovingly detailed sunsets, the growing of greengrass [sic], the sweep of land and rivers, the outgrowth of stone.<br /><br />However, the story slowly grew on me as I read because these came to be real people, not just an amalgam of annoying character traits. They are closely bound to each other not simply by family ties and obligations but their chosen profession (horse breeding and selling) and the land itself. This was a time and place when human fortune rose and fell with a good year or a bad one and yet a living was hard to grind out because of government interference. Reading about how the family pulled together was very touching.<br /><br />Running through this story like a golden river through a rocky mountain is the tale of a boy’s relentless, heartfelt love for his filly, a spirited creature he longs to tame, love and make his own. Ken’s feelings are presented with such searing intensity that it is almost embarrassing to read, like coming across two lovers caught in a passionate embrace. Here is the all-consuming love that children often bring to the unlikeliest of objects—a doll, a stuffed toy, a ragged animal they claim as a pet—made real and palpable. That love and the details of its progress are what make this book a classic because affection like that is universal and understood by anyone who has ever felt it for another.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14151164961331288785">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <a href="/book/show/164542.My_Friend_Flicka" title="Paperback 9780060512620" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/39869338-kelly-haacke?shelf=children-s-literature" class="actionLinkLite">children-s-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1255736263">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3721719608402040916">I chose the book, "My Friend Flicka" By Mary O'Hara. This realistic fiction book intended for children ages 7 or 8 and up is about a young boy who spends his days on his family's ranch and one day meets this horse named Flicka. His dad however does not like the strong bond between his son and the horse, however towards the end of the story the fierce loyalty between the horse and him almost costs the boy his life. I gave this book a rating of 5 out of 5 because I liked the book and I thought it</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3721719608402040916">I chose the book, "My Friend Flicka" By Mary O'Hara. This realistic fiction book intended for children ages 7 or 8 and up is about a young boy who spends his days on his family's ranch and one day meets this horse named Flicka. His dad however does not like the strong bond between his son and the horse, however towards the end of the story the fierce loyalty between the horse and him almost costs the boy his life. I gave this book a rating of 5 out of 5 because I liked the book and I thought it was very effective. This book is also based off of the movie "Flicka." The language of this book I thought was appropriate for this age group and it was very easy to read. Although there were no illustrations in this book I think it is still effective because it allows children to use there imagination and create their own vision of the story between the father, son and the horse. There was also no color throughout the book either, it was just in black and white. I liked the theme of the book because it's about the strong bond/love between a boy and his horse, and as the bond grows stronger, the conflict between the boy and his father grows bigger. I think this book would be appealing to children because if they love animals or horses in general then they might be interested in the book, to see what happens. Lastly, I would definitely use this book while working with children because I really think this book is interesting, and I love the movie version of it too, and I would definitely show the movie as well. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17236082583989051835"><strong>"It couldn't be done but the darn fool didn't know it and went ahead and did it"</strong><br /><br />Two separate lives, of a kid and an animal, are about to change for good.<br /><br />First published in 1941, this beautifully written easy read tells you about the bond between men and the most graceful animal to ever set foot on the soil - Horses. The bond that emerges out of love, responsibility, companionship and respect. Mary O'Hara takes you to Wyoming suburbs where Rob McLaughlin, a horse rancher, is living a simple but h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17236082583989051835"><strong>"It couldn't be done but the darn fool didn't know it and went ahead and did it"</strong><br /><br />Two separate lives, of a kid and an animal, are about to change for good.<br /><br />First published in 1941, this beautifully written easy read tells you about the bond between men and the most graceful animal to ever set foot on the soil - Horses. The bond that emerges out of love, responsibility, companionship and respect. Mary O'Hara takes you to Wyoming suburbs where Rob McLaughlin, a horse rancher, is living a simple but hard life with his wife and two sons. There is nothing substantially striking about the plot. The story is all about a journey of a boy from aimless day dreaming and time wasting to the path of responsibility and practicality. Journey of an animal from craziness to absolute loyalty. <br /><br />If you are finding escape from all those mentally challenging plots and looking for a simple one, this is your typical park-bench read.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_266488923">

<span id="freeTextContainer16382894578291640538">When I was a kid I had a terrible cold. My dad brought me home this book. I remember being totally engrossed and forgetting for a while how sick I was. It is the touching story of a boy who believes in a horse that everyone else says is loco (crazy). I was touched by his devotion to Flicka. Reading this will always be a found memory.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1195867543303572108">This is a good story for the young horse lover. The original book is very old and is written in the style of it's time, which could make it a difficult read for younger kids. It tells the story of a young boy who is having trouble fitting in at school and with his family due to his constant day-dreaming. The boy debates with his family about how having a horse of his own will make him more responsible, but he must prove it. Flicka is a young wild filly who the boy picks out as his own, and tells his tale of trying to break-in and befriend Flicka.<br /><br />I read this book in high school and found it a little slow. It's not incredibly exciting, but it is a classic that will draw horse-lovers. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/850660020?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 10, 2014</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer850660020">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1904093872729718477"> My Friend Flicka. Oh, how I wanted to live on a ranch in Wyoming! I lived on a pony farm in central New York state, but still wanted to ride the range with Ken, the hero of the story, when I was a girl. One of the best horse books of my youth. I was fascinated by the lives of the family, the boys went to boarding school because the ranch was remote, and Ken came home with poor grades while his brother had an excellent report. "If I only had a colt," Ken keeps saying.<br /> A fine book. I have my copy</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1904093872729718477"> My Friend Flicka. Oh, how I wanted to live on a ranch in Wyoming! I lived on a pony farm in central New York state, but still wanted to ride the range with Ken, the hero of the story, when I was a girl. One of the best horse books of my youth. I was fascinated by the lives of the family, the boys went to boarding school because the ranch was remote, and Ken came home with poor grades while his brother had an excellent report. "If I only had a colt," Ken keeps saying.<br /> A fine book. I have my copy from 1967 (sixty-cents!). I highly recommend this story, it stands the test of time.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1427070704">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1427070704" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/45149199-emma-filbrun" class="left imgcol" title="Emma Filbrun"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Emma Filbrun" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1427070704?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/45149199-emma-filbrun" class="user" title="Emma Filbrun">Emma Filbrun</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/164542.My_Friend_Flicka" title="Paperback 9780060512620" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1427070704">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12985035842447671780">I first read My Friend Flicka a number of years ago, and really enjoyed it. When one of my boys chose it for oral reading practice recently, I was looking forward to enjoying an old friend again. I must say, though, it wasn’t what I remembered. I remembered the high points of the story, but as it turns out, this book is more what I would call a psychological book than a story. It is definitely an adult book rather than a children’s book.<br /><br /><p>Read my full review <a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://learningresourcedirectory.com/my-friend-flicka">here</a>.</p></span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <a href="/user/show/5698638-wendy-orr" class="user" title="Wendy Orr">Wendy Orr</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/164542.My_Friend_Flicka" title="Paperback 9780060512620" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5698638-wendy-orr?shelf=animals" class="actionLinkLite">animals</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5698638-wendy-orr?shelf=american-literature" class="actionLinkLite">american-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5698638-wendy-orr?shelf=american-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">american-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1275820196">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1971995570164729381">One of my childhood favourites, it was fascinating to reread this and discover other layers that I had completely missed - I had no idea that it was so much the story of a marriage, and of parenting, as well as the 'boy wants a horse' that I'd remembered. The 1930's pronouncements on the evils of daydreaming and how psychiatrists need to cure it, made me cringe, but that's part of the interest of reading an 80 year old book. The relationship between the boy and the filly is still beautiful, and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1971995570164729381">One of my childhood favourites, it was fascinating to reread this and discover other layers that I had completely missed - I had no idea that it was so much the story of a marriage, and of parenting, as well as the 'boy wants a horse' that I'd remembered. The 1930's pronouncements on the evils of daydreaming and how psychiatrists need to cure it, made me cringe, but that's part of the interest of reading an 80 year old book. The relationship between the boy and the filly is still beautiful, and the book was still deeply satisfying.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_743011222">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743011222" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/24758991-lisa" class="left imgcol" title="Lisa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1381978282p2/24758991.jpg" alt="Lisa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/743011222?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/24758991-lisa" class="user" title="Lisa">Lisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/164542.My_Friend_Flicka" title="Paperback 9780060512620" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/24758991-lisa?shelf=five-star-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">five-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/24758991-lisa?shelf=top-ten" class="actionLinkLite">top-ten</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/24758991-lisa?shelf=top-25" class="actionLinkLite">top-25</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer743011222">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4351155214216823202">(This review is for people who have read the book. Spoiler alert)<br /><br />I love Flicka. I'd forgotten how sweet she was. My heart just hurts and flutters when I think of her<br />waiting for Ken at the fence, hopping after him on three legs, wasting away, lying in the cold water, head up as Gus came closer, resting in the sling in the rain with Rob and Nell keeping watch. Such great scenes! There are no words for what this book means to me. It was my fantasy all my life ... still is.<br /><br /><em> My Friend Flicka </em> challen</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4351155214216823202">(This review is for people who have read the book. Spoiler alert)<br /><br />I love Flicka. I'd forgotten how sweet she was. My heart just hurts and flutters when I think of her<br />waiting for Ken at the fence, hopping after him on three legs, wasting away, lying in the cold water, head up as Gus came closer, resting in the sling in the rain with Rob and Nell keeping watch. Such great scenes! There are no words for what this book means to me. It was my fantasy all my life ... still is.<br /><br /><em> My Friend Flicka </em> challenges me every time I read it. This time I see that you can't wait until a child becomes responsible to give him responsibility, holding a carrot out for him saying, you get this when you measure up. It's the giving of responsibility that teaches the child, that brings him up to measure, if the mentor is invested and patient and willing to risk. Learning responsibility is messy. It's so much easier to say, when you can do it without mess, then I'll give it to you. Rob McLaughlin, the father, was tough, but he wanted a friendship with his son. In his mind, Ken should prove himself first, but he opted to give him the horse because he didn't know what else to do, and he didn't want to lose a relationship with him. <br /><br /> "The achievement was Flicka and the winning of her friendship. He had a horse now. ... He couldn't ride her yet, but she was his because she had given herself to him.<br /> She loved his hands, his touch, his caresses. She loved to have him stand at her head, facing her, his hands lightly holding her cheeks. They looked into each other's eyes as lovers look. He spent all the time with her that he could.<br /> While she stood eating her oats, his hands smoothed the satin-soft skin under her mane. It had a nap as deep as plush. He played with her long, cream-colored tresses; arranged her forelock neatly between her eyes. She was a bit dish-faced, like an Arab, with eyes set far apart. Ken kept a currycomb and brush in the crotch of the cottonwood tree, and lightly groomed and brushed her. Flicka enjoyed this. As he moved about her, first on one side, then the other, kneeling down to brush her legs and polish her small hoofs which had the color and sheen of cream-colored marble, she turned her head to him, and always, if she could, rested her muzzle on him. Ken grew used to the feel of the warm, moist lips against his shoulder or back, and his mother complained of all the polo shirts he dirtied tending to Flicka."<br /><br />The last paragraph of the book is epic.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4351155214216823202">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_597975267">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/597975267" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19704755-patricia" class="left imgcol" title="Patricia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446933622p2/19704755.jpg" alt="Patricia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/597975267?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19704755-patricia" class="user" title="Patricia">Patricia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/164542.My_Friend_Flicka" title="Paperback 9780060512620" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19704755-patricia?shelf=contemporary-ending" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-ending</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19704755-patricia?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19704755-patricia?shelf=westerns" class="actionLinkLite">westerns</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19704755-patricia?shelf=wyoming" class="actionLinkLite">wyoming</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19704755-patricia?shelf=read-2013-or-before" class="actionLinkLite">read-2013-or-before</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer597975267">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1528537716136352613">A book to read, and to re-read, and to read yet again.<br />I attended college in Laramie, Wyoming, just miles from where this book is set. I did my Master's research in the mountains that got named "The Never Summer Range", and indeed, there were even then glacial lakes and snow fields at the tops. On a more grisly note, there are abandoned mine shafts where ranchers dumped dead animals, and where at least one woman dumped her husband after she murdered him.<br />I confess, when Mrs. Dewey read this to us</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1528537716136352613">A book to read, and to re-read, and to read yet again.<br />I attended college in Laramie, Wyoming, just miles from where this book is set. I did my Master's research in the mountains that got named "The Never Summer Range", and indeed, there were even then glacial lakes and snow fields at the tops. On a more grisly note, there are abandoned mine shafts where ranchers dumped dead animals, and where at least one woman dumped her husband after she murdered him.<br />I confess, when Mrs. Dewey read this to us in third grade, I only kind of listened. It was about a world I was unfamiliar with, and I couldn't get any sort of grip on the story. By the next time I read it, I totally understood Ken. I understood Flicka too. But it was still just a story. It wasn't until quite a few years later that I found myself puzzling through just what happened that fateful summer. Not just to Ken, but to his whole family, because in gaining the horse, and nearly losing the horse, in nearly losing his life, Ken gets swept up into a "drifting place" where nothing really matters anymore. In nearly losing Ken, his family and Flicka come to realize that he is vital, and losable.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1528537716136352613">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kY07Ti7ckmLwbwTDp7X9zSVpgiSFGXRcxEydOurDNO70WQSd3A6GmHy3cHjZ1Bt/bJ5BPczEM/auRZioJlbCqw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

This is a period piece--a threatened puppy is described, for example, as &amp;quot;a blinking pygmy who gallantly essayed to growl defiance&amp;quot;--and that touch of fustian is all part of Terhune\'s enduring charm. Because the stories didn\'t originally appear together, there\'s considerable repetition: nearly every story with a fight scene has the same authorial mini-lecture on the difference in fighting technique between collies and bulldogs. But Lad is a character who has poked his muzzle into a million hearts, and new generations of dog lovers will also appreciate his loyalty and courage.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/95600.Mary_O_Hara">About Mary O'Hara</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/95600.Mary_O_Hara"><img alt="95600" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1302934828p2/95600.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14473425948362431836">Mary O’Hara Alsop, an American author, screenwriter, and composer, was born July 10, 1885, in Cape May, N.J., to Reese Fell Alsop and Mary Lee (Spring). She grew up in Brooklyn Heights, N.Y., where her father was an Episcopal clergyman.<br /><br />In 1905, Ms. O'hara married Kent Kane Parrot, whom she later divorced. Her second marriage to Helge Sture-Vasa from Sweden in 1922 also ended in divorce in 1947. Ms</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14473425948362431836">Mary O’Hara Alsop, an American author, screenwriter, and composer, was born July 10, 1885, in Cape May, N.J., to Reese Fell Alsop and Mary Lee (Spring). She grew up in Brooklyn Heights, N.Y., where her father was an Episcopal clergyman.<br /><br />In 1905, Ms. O'hara married Kent Kane Parrot, whom she later divorced. Her second marriage to Helge Sture-Vasa from Sweden in 1922 also ended in divorce in 1947. Ms. O’Hara had two children from her first marriage, Mary O’Hara who died of skin cancer during her teens, and Kent Kane, Jr.<br /><br />Ms. O’Hara moved to California after her first marriage where she became a screenwriter during the silent film era through the advent of talking movies.<br /><br />In 1930, during her second marriage, Ms O’Hara moved to a ranch in Wyoming where she wrote her three novels, the classic “My Friend Flicka,” and the sequels “Thunderhead” and “Green Grass of Wyoming,” about the McLaughlin family and the younger son and his horse, Flicka.<br /><br />In addition to writing, Ms O’Hara was a successful composer and published numerous songs for the piano. She also wrote a musical play called "The Catch Colt" which she later turned into a novel, first published in 1979 in Great Britain. The rights to performing this as a play or a musical can still be obtained through Dramatists Play Services, New York.<br /><br />While she claimed her first love was musical composition, she continued writing fiction and nonfiction.<br /><br />A year after her divorce from her second husband in 1947, Ms O’Hara returned to the east coast where she lived in Connecticut until 1968. She died Oct. 14, 1980, in Chevy Chase, Md. Her literary works are maintained by Georgetown University in Washington, D.C.<br />(sources: Current Biography, 1944; Contemporary Authors, 1981)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14473425948362431836">...more</a>

    </div>
